I'm running out but wanted to share an awesome idea from my colleague
@chrisfilo:

The basic idea is that we could use continuous integration (eg, circle.ci)
to do docker2singularity image conversion, as many docker images are hosted
on github and have these kind of checks. It would be triggered by a docker
hub hook, or just pushing to a branch, and then push the images to a google
drive that would get indexed by singularity hub. For more docker (base)
images we could use a lightweight repo (something like conda forge) that
would do the same. This would mean that a user could easily add their image
to singularity hub without doing any kind of manual work (creating an
account,logging in, clicking upload) by simply adding a line to their
circle.yml (the continuous integration spec) file.

I find this idea very awesome :)

On Sat, Jul 16, 2016 at 9:43 AM, vanessa s <vso...@gmail.com> wrote:

> Oh I understand - so having the singularity hub have support for having
> containers hosted in other areas (eg, instead of "upload container" you
> would link to a container URL in something like Google drive. Then the shub
> tool would be able to retrieve the image in whatever places are supported -
> that's a cool idea! I think we will definitely want to think about options
> like this to give a researcher maximum flexibility for how he/she wants to
> host images. If hosted at an external URL the hub would still need to
> retrieve and process the image to get meta data. The one issue that comes
> to mind is keeping meta data about the image up to date with the image
> itself. If the hub is holding some parameters about an image, and then its
> changed in the drive, there would need to be a check of the md5 sum, and if
> it doesn't match, the container information updated on the hub before using
> it. The other issue that is problematic here is if a user hosted image goes
> away. Let's say I am using an image from your Google Drive, then you leave
> your institution and leave the free space, and then I can no longer use it
> in my workflow. Requiring the user to upload it to the hub first ensures
> that doesn't happen.
>
> Is it more an issue of where to store images for the hub, that it maps
> onto something that could be mapped locally? That would be a +1 for drive.
> If you are concerned about having a central repository for images we could
> also consider something like S3, etc.
>
>
> On Sat, Jul 16, 2016 at 9:33 AM, Gregory M. Kurtzer <gmku...@lbl.gov>
> wrote:
>
>> Sorry for not being clear, also the idea comes with only a rudimentary
>> understanding of the architecture you are building.. So it may not be
>> relevant.
>>
>> But the idea is based on the following being true... The command line
>> tool (let's call it SHUB for now - Singulrity Hub) will download and run a
>> particular workflow compromised of one or more containers and link them
>> together in a pipeline to achieve a predetermined workflow. This command
>> line tool will contact the HUB and use some identifier string to identify a
>> particular workflow. That workflow will encapsulated in a JSON (or other)
>> description file which will include not only the workflow pipeline, but
>> also the location to download the container images from.
>>
>> My idea is based on the above scenario being accurate. It would simply
>> use the Google Drive's API (or one of several command line tools) to share
>> the image in drive (which will reveal a publicly accessible URL) that can
>> be used within the JSON description for 'SHUB' to download the containers
>> from and then execute the workflow. I still think that SHUB should properly
>> cache the containers locally (possibly indexed by MD5?) so subsequent SHUB
>> calls won't have to re-download the containers. It may also be good to
>> provide a SHUB --download option so user can prefetch the containers from a
>> dedicated data transfer node (DTN) before running the job.
>>
>> The HUB system itself will be responsible for staging the containers into
>> drive (and thus the uploads will go through it), but then it will upload
>> them to drive and all subsequent requests of those containers do not have
>> to funnel the data IO through the HUB.
>>
>> Thoughts?
>>
>>
>> On Sat, Jul 16, 2016 at 9:03 AM, vanessa s <vso...@gmail.com> wrote:
>>
>>> Could you explain more what you mean by that? What singularity hub adds
>>> isn't serving/storage of images, but connecting them and serving the
>>> workflows. Are you thinking about some kind of local API (in some command
>>> line tool) to do something with just the images?
>>>
